وكسبُهُ له فإن كاتب قنين له زوجين، فولدت دخلَ الولد في كتابتها وكسبه لها وكسبُهُ له ) : أي كَسْبُ ولدِ المكاتب يكونُ للمكاتب ؛ لأنَّ الولد كسبه، وكسب الولد كسب كسبه".

(فإن كاتب قنين له زوجين فولدت دخلَ الولد في كتابتها ، وكسبه لها) : أي زوج أمتَهُ من عبده فكاتبهما ، فولدت ولداً دَخَلَ الولد في كتابة الأم، وكسبُهُ للأم ؛ لأنَّ الولد يتبع الأم في الرق والعتق وفروعه.

قلت : نعم ؛ إلا أنّ له في مكاتبه يداً كالحرّ، وذلك يكفي لثبوت النسب منه عند الدعوى ، وإن لم يحلّ وطؤه كما في الجارية المشتركة، وجارية الابن إذا وطئها الأبُ وادعى الأب. كذا في شرح العَيْنِي

[١] قوله : كسب كسبه ؛ وكان كسب الولد قبل الدعوى ، فلا ينقطع بالدعوة اختصاصه ؛ أي اختصاص المكاتب بكسب ولده ، وكذلك إذا ولدت المكاتبة من زنا أو زوجها دخل الولد في كتابتها ؛ لأنّ الولد المولود يسري إليه الصفات الشرعية الثابتة في الأمر كالتدبير والاستيلاد والحرية والملك ، فإذا سرى إليها صار حكمه كحكم أمه فكانت هــي أحـق بـه وبكسبه ؛ لأنه جزؤها ، وقد انقطـع حـق المولى عنه. كذا في «التبيين»(۲).

[٢] قوله : في كتابة الأم ؛ بناءً على أنَّ الأوصاف القارة الشرعية في الأمهات تسري إلى الأولاد. كذا في شرح العيني(۳).

[٣]قوله : لأنّ الولد يتبع الأم ؛ وإنّما كان تبعية الأم أرجح ؛ لأنه جزء منها، بحيث يقرض منها بالمقراض. كذا في ((العناية(٤).

[٤] قوله : وفروعه ؛ يعني الكتابة والتدبير والاستيلاد فإنّ هذه الأوصاف القارة الشرعية في الأمهات تسري إلى الأولاد، وإذا سرت كتابتها إلى ولدها لم يجز بيعه كما في «التبيين».
Husn al-Dirayah li-Awakhir Sharh al-Wiqayah. And his earning is for him. If he makes a kitabah contract with a couple of slaves (qinin) he owns, and [the wife] gives birth, the child enters her kitabah, and his earning is for her, and his earning is for him: i.e., the earning of the child of the mukatab belongs to the mukatab because the child is his earning, and the earning of the child is the earning of his earning. (If he makes a kitabah contract with a couple of slaves he owns, and [the wife] gives birth, the child enters her kitabah, and his earning is for her): i.e., he married his slave woman to his slave and then made a kitabah contract with both of them, so she gave birth to a child; the child enters the kitabah of the mother, and his earning is for the mother because the child follows the mother in slavery, freedom, and their branches. I say: Yes, but he has in his [the mukatab's] hand authority like a free person, and that suffices for establishing lineage from him upon claim, even if his intercourse is not permissible, as in the case of a jointly owned slave girl and the slave girl of a son when the father has intercourse with her and the father claims [the child]. Thus in Sharh al-Ayni. [Footnote 1: His statement: 'the earning of his earning'; and the earning of the child was before the claim, so his right is not cut off by the claim; i.e., the mukatab's right to his child's earning, and likewise if a female mukatab gives birth from zina or from her husband, the child enters her kitabah because the child is subject to the legal attributes established in the course of the matter, such as tadbir, istilad, freedom, and ownership. So when it runs to her, his ruling becomes like her ruling, so she is more entitled to him and his earning because he is part of her, and the right of the master is cut off from him. Thus in al-Tabyin.] [Footnote 2: His statement: 'in the mother's kitabah'; based on the fact that the permanent legal attributes in mothers run to the children. Thus in Sharh al-Ayni.] [Footnote 3: His statement: 'because the child follows the mother'; the mother's precedence is because he is part of her, to the extent that he could be excised from her with scissors. Thus in al-Inayah.] [Footnote 4: His statement: 'and their branches'; meaning kitabah, tadbir, and istilad, for these permanent legal attributes in the mothers run to the children, and if her kitabah runs to her child, it is not permissible to sell him, as in al-Tabyin.]
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the mukatab's child with two additional rulings. First, the earning of a mukatab's child belongs to the mukatab himself, because the child is his earning (kasb) and the earning of his earning. Second, if a mukatab owns a married pair of slaves (qinin) and makes a kitabah contract with both of them, and the wife then gives birth to a child, that child enters the mother's kitabah, and the child's earning belongs to the mother, not the father. This is because the child follows the mother in legal attributes such as slavery, freedom, and their branches (including kitabah). The mother's precedence is stronger because the child is a part of her. The text then applies the same principle to a female mukatab who gives birth from zina or from her husband: the child enters her kitabah because the legal attributes (like tadbir, istilad, freedom, ownership) run from the mother to the child, overriding the master's rights. This ruling is based on the idea that permanent legal attributes (awṣāf qārrah) in the mother run to the offspring.

Key Terms
قنين (qinin): A male and female slave who are married to each other.
كسب (kasb): Earnings or acquisition; here specifically the child's income or labor product.
أوصاف قارة (awṣāf qārrah): Permanent legal attributes such as slavery, freedom, tadbir, istilad, and kitabah that transfer from the mother to her child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They belong to the father (mukatab)
B) They belong to the mother
C) They belong to the master
D) The child is free and keeps his earnings

Key Takeaway
A child's legal status follows the mother's permanent attributes, including kitabah; the mukatab's child is his earning but in the qinin case the mother's rights prevail.

The Mukatib's Child: Earnings and Entry into Mother's Kitabah
Explaining a mukatib's child's earnings and entry into mother's kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatib's child's earnings and explain why the child enters the mother's kitabah.

Core Idea
A mukatib's child follows the mother in legal status; his earnings belong to the father as his kash.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi tradition regarding a mukatib (a slave under a manumission contract) who has a child with his wife—also a mukatibah. The central question: who gets the child's earnings, and does the child enter the mother's kitabah? The answer rests on the principle that permanent legal attributes (al-awsaf al-qarra) flow from mother to child, and that the child is considered part of the mother's earning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (a mukatib's child from his mukatibah wife) and the core rulings: (a) the child enters the mother's kitabah, (b) the child's earnings belong to the mukatib father (as his kash).
The child is treated as part of the mother's kitabah, not a separate contract.
2
Understand the Principle of Permanent Attributes
Recognize the key legal principle: permanent attributes (kitabah, tadbir, istilad, freedom, slavery) in the mother flow to her child. This is why the child shares the mother's status as a mukatib.
This principle is derived from the general maxim that offspring follow the mother in legal status.
3
Apply to Child's Earnings
Connect the principle to earnings: since the child is part of the mother (her 'part'), and the mother's earnings belong to her, the child's earnings also belong to her. But since the mother is a mukatibah, her earnings ultimately go to her husband (the mukatib) as his kash.
The father's right to the child's earnings is because the child is his kash (earning).
4
Note the Exception for Paternity Claim
Observe that despite the child following the mother, the mukatib father retains the right to claim paternity (due to his 'hand' like a free person), even though sexual intercourse with a mukatibah is not permissible.
This exception shows that the father's paternity rights are preserved.

"(فإن كاتب قنين له زوجين فولدتْ دخلَ الولد في كتابتها ، وكسبه لها) : أي زوج أمتَهُ من عبده فكاتبهما ، فولدت ولداً دَخَلَ الولد في كتابة الأم، وكسبُهُ للأم ؛ لأنَّ الولد يتبع الأم في الرق والعتق وفروعه.

And his earnings are for him. So if he makes a mukatib of a slave couple who have two spouses, and she gives birth, the child enters into her kitabah, and its earnings are for her, and his earnings are for him. That is: the earnings of the mukatib's child are for the mukatib because the child is his earning, and the earnings of the child are the earning of his earning. (If he makes a mukatib of a slave couple who have two spouses and she gives birth, the child enters into the mother's kitabah, and its earnings are for the mother) because the child follows the mother in slavery, freedom, and their branches. I say: Yes, except that he (the mukatib) has a hand like a free person over his mukatib, and that suffices for establishing lineage from him upon claim, even if his intercourse is not permissible, as in the case of a jointly-owned slave-girl, and the slave-girl of a son if the father has intercourse and claims paternity. Thus in al-'Ayni's commentary. [1] His saying: 'the earning of his earning' – the child's earning before the claim is not cut off by the claim's specificity, i.e., the mukatib's specificity over his child's earnings. Likewise, if a mukatibah gives birth from fornication or her husband, the child enters her kitabah because the legal attributes that are stable in the matter, such as tadbir, istilad, freedom, and ownership, flow to the newborn. So when they flow to her, his ruling becomes like that of his mother, so she is more entitled to him and his earnings because he is her part, and the master's right over him is cut off. Thus in al-Tabyin. [2] His saying: 'in the mother's kitabah' is based on the idea that the permanent legal attributes in mothers flow to children. Thus in al-'Ayni's commentary. [3] His saying: 'because the child follows the mother'; the mother's priority is stronger because he is part of her, to the extent that he could be cut from her with scissors. Thus in al-'Inaya. [4] His saying: 'and their branches' means kitabah, tadbir, and istilad; these permanent legal attributes in mothers flow to children. If her kitabah flows to her child, it is not permissible to sell him just as it is not permissible to sell his mother. Thus in al-'Inaya.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling from the matn (likely al-Wiqaya) regarding a mukatib's child. The core ruling: if a mukatib (a slave contracted for manumission) has a child from his wife (who is also a mukatibah), the child enters into the mother's kitabah (contract of manumission). Consequently, the child's earnings belong to the mother (and ultimately to the mukatib father as his kash, since the child is his earning). The reasoning is that the child follows the mother in legal status (slavery/freedom) and the branches thereof (kitabah, tadbir, istilad). The commentator adds a nuance: the mukatib has the legal hand (yad) of a free person for purposes of claiming paternity, even though his intercourse is not permissible (because he is a slave). This is similar to cases of a jointly-owned slave-girl or a son's slave-girl where the father can claim paternity. Additionally, the child's earnings before any claim of manumission are not interrupted; the mukatib retains the right to those earnings. This ruling is based on the general principle that permanent legal attributes (al-awsaf al-qarra al-shar'iyyah) in mothers flow to their children.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
كسب (kash): Earnings, especially referring to the income or acquisitions of a mukatib or his child.
الأوصاف القارة (al-awsaf al-qarra): Permanent legal attributes that are stable in a person, such as freedom, slavery, kitabah, tadbir, and istilad, which flow from parent to child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The earnings go to the master.
B) The earnings go to the child itself.
C) The earnings belong to the mukatib father as his kash.
D) The earnings are divided between the mukatib and his wife.

Key Takeaway
A mukatib's child enters the mother's kitabah, and the child's earnings belong to the mukatib father because the child is his kash and permanent attributes flow from the mother.

‘Uqr of a Mukatab: Purchase vs Marriage
Ruling on ‘uqr for mukatab in purchase vs marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ‘uqr for a mukatab in purchase and marriage cases and explain the rationale for the difference.

Core Idea
A mukatab’s ‘uqr is immediate in purchase but deferred in marriage because purchase is part of his earning capacity.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah addresses a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: when a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) has intercourse with a female slave he purchased, the ‘uqr (dower equivalent) is due immediately. But if he marries a female slave and has intercourse, the ‘uqr is taken only after he becomes free. The commentator explains this difference by analyzing the nature of purchase (trade) versus marriage (personal status) and the mukatab’s ability to pay during the kitabah period. A strong proof from ijma of the Companions is cited for the free man’s case, and the mukatab is distinguished from the free man due to his inability to pay immediately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the two cases: (1) the mukatab purchases a female slave and has intercourse, then the slave is claimed; (2) the mukatab marries a female slave and has intercourse, then she is claimed.
Both cases involve a defect in title (istihqaq) after intercourse.
2
State the ruling for each
For purchase: ‘uqr is taken immediately. For marriage: ‘uqr is taken when the mukatab becomes free (at emancipation).
The matn says: 'أخذ عقرها في الحال' for purchase, and 'أخذ حين عتق' for marriage.
3
Analyze the proof and distinction
The commentator anticipates an objection: why not analogize the mukatab to a free man (who is not liable for immediate ‘uqr due to ijma)? The answer: the free man’s case is an exception to qiyas, based on ijma of the Companions. The mukatab is not similar because he cannot pay immediately, so the ruling follows original qiyas (or istihsan) leading to deferment in marriage. But in purchase, the hadd falls, so ‘uqr is obligatory as part of trade consequences.
The key distinction is that purchase is within the mukatab's earning capacity ('kash'), marriage is not.
4
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
In purchase, the mukatab has permission to trade; intercourse with a purchased slave, even without explicit permission, is considered within trade. Therefore, the ‘uqr is due immediately from his earnings. In marriage, no such permission exists; the mukatab cannot pay mahr or ‘uqr during kitabah, so it is deferred until freedom.
The text states 'لولا الشراء لما سقط الحد' meaning without purchase, the hadd would not fall, indicating that the purchase triggers the obligation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
According to Abu Hanifa, if the mukatab pays the ‘uqr, he can seek recourse (رجوع) against the woman who misled him (by claiming she was free). This is mentioned in the commentary as 'يرجع عليها عنده'.
This indicates a difference among the Hanafi imams, although the primary ruling on timing is consistent.

The distinction is that were it not for the purchase, the hadd would not fall; and as long as the hadd does not fall, the 'uqr is not obligatory, so it is among the consequences of trade, so it is established regarding the master's right. And it appears that it is required that the tenth or half does not fall below ten dirhams; if it falls short, it must be completed to ten, because mahr does not fall below ten, whether it is mahr al-mithl or m usamma. And it is said regarding slave girls: one looks at the like of that slave in beauty and whose master — how much would she be married for? So it is considered by that, and that is the chosen view. And he may not marry a woman without the master's permission; nonetheless, if he marries, the mahr is taken from him when he becomes free. Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah, discussing the ruling of 'uqr (dower equivalent) for a mukatab (a slave who has contracted manumission) in two scenarios: intercourse with a female slave he purchased, and intercourse with a female slave he married. The commentator begins by presenting the matn (core text) from Al-Wiqayah: 'If he (the mukatab) has intercourse with a female slave he owns and she is claimed (by someone else), or with a fasid (defective) purchase and she is returned, then her 'uqr is taken immediately, like the authorized trader. And if he married and had intercourse, it is taken when he becomes free.' The sharh then expands on this by addressing a potential objection: why not analogize this case to that of a free man who, by ijma of the Companions, is exempted from paying immediate 'uqr because he relied on a mistaken belief? The commentator explains that the free man's case is an exception to qiyas based on ijma, and the mukatab's case is not similar because the free man can pay compensation immediately, whereas the slave cannot. The effective cause ('illa) for deferring 'uqr in the free man's case is the inability to pay immediately, which applies to the mukatab as well, so the same ruling of deferment applies in the marriage scenario. However, in the purchase scenario, the 'uqr is immediate because the hadd punishment falls (since intercourse is presumed permissible due to ownership), and thus the 'uqr is due as part of the trade consequences, which the mukatab can fulfill through his kitabah earnings. The definition of 'uqr is then explained: for free women it is mahr al-mithl, for slaves it is a tenth of the value (if virgin) or half tenth (if non-virgin), with a minimum of ten dirhams. The commentator also clarifies that permission to purchase implies permission to intercourse, so the 'uqr is immediate even if the mukatab had permission to buy. But marriage requires separate permission from the master; if permission is not given, the mahr is deferred until freedom because the mukatab cannot pay during kitabah. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh regarding the financial obligations of a mukatab. The passage relies on the principle that the mukatab's earning capacity during kitabah is limited to trade, not marriage, hence the differentiation.

Key Terms
عقر (‘uqr): In this passage, 'uqr refers to the financial compensation due for sexual intercourse with a female slave when ownership is not established or is defective, akin to mahr for a free woman.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of kitabah with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for his freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is the ‘uqr taken from a mukatab if he marries a female slave without the master's permission and has intercourse with her?
A) Immediately, because the hadd falls
B) At the time of emancipation, because marriage is not part of his earning capacity
C) Only if the mukatab pays the value first
D) Never, because the mukatab cannot be liable for ‘uqr

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's ‘uqr is immediate in purchase (trade) and deferred in marriage (non-trade), based on the difference in earning capacity and the fall of hadd.

Ruling on a Mukatab's Tadbir for His Own Slave
Ruling on tadbir by a mukatab for his own slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a mukatab's tadbir for his own slave and explain the mukatab's options upon the master's death.

Core Idea
A mukatab can validly declare his own slave as mudabbar; upon the master's death he chooses incapacity or continuing the kitaba.

This lesson deals with the validity of tadbir (postponed manumission) when performed by a mukatab (a slave under a kitaba contract) for his own slave. The key question is whether a mukatab, who is himself not fully free, can make such a declaration. The Hanafi position clarifies that it is valid, and the mukatab is given an option when his master dies. Understanding this ruling requires knowing the capacity of a mukatab over his property and the nature of tadbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: a mukatab making tadbir for his own slave. The ruling: valid (sahih). The tadbir takes effect upon the mukatab's own manumission.
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the mukatab's option upon the master's death
When the mukatab's master dies poor, the mukatab has a choice: either declare himself incapable (ajz nafsahu) and become mudabbar himself, or continue the kitaba and pay two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitaba payment.
The option applies only if the master dies poor.
3
Understand the key terms
Tadbir: a declaration that a slave will be free upon the declarant's death. Ajz nafsahu: the mukatab's declaration of incapacity to fulfill the kitaba, which transforms him into a mudabbar.
These terms are specific to the Hanafi fiqh of manumission.
4
Distinguish the 'uqr discussion
The commentary includes a marginal note linking kitaba to 'uqr through purchase, but this is not directly relevant to the tadbir ruling. The main ruling stands independent of that discussion.
Avoid confusing the 'uqr analogy with the core ruling.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a mukatab (a slave under kitaba) may validly make his own slave a mudabbar (postponed manumission). Upon the death of the mukatab's master (the original owner), the mukatab has a choice: either he declares himself incapable (ajz nafsahu) and becomes mudabbar (so he and his slave become free upon the master's death), or he continues the kitaba and pays two-thirds of his value (or two-thirds of the kitaba payment) if the master dies poor. The commentary then attempts to connect this with the previous discussion about 'uqr, but this seems to be a marginal note. The reliable rule is that a mukatab can declare his own slave as mudabbar, and the mukatab has an option when his master dies. The text also includes a comparison that the kitaba leads to purchase, which leads to dropping of hadd, which leads to 'uqr, while marriage does not. However, the main ruling is straightforward: the tadbir is valid and the mukatab has a choice.

تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death; a mudabbar is a slave so designated.
عجز نفسه (ajz nafsahu): The mukatab's declaration of incapacity to fulfill the kitaba, which may result in his becoming mudabbar.

Tadbir of a Mukatab: Validity and Options Upon Master's Death
Ruling on tadbir of a mukatab with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tadbir of a mukatab is valid and explain the mukatab's option to either become mudabbar or continue kitabah at reduced payment, including the rational proof linking kitabah to 'aqr.

Core Idea
Tadbir of a mukatab is valid, giving the mukatab a choice: become mudabbar or continue kitabah at two-thirds value.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario in slave emancipation: a master who already has a mukatab (a slave under kitabah) makes a tadbir declaration, promising freedom upon his death. The question arises whether the tadbir is valid and what happens if the master dies without other property. The text affirms validity and outlines the mukatab's options. It also tackles a potential objection regarding the 'aqr (dower) using a logical causal chain, distinguishing kitabah from marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage begins by stating that the tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death) of a mukatab is valid (sahih). Identify this as the core legal ruling.
The validity is affirmed despite the existing kitabah contract.
2
Determine the Operative Scenario
The scenario considered is when the master dies poor (i.e., with no other property to cover the tadbir). The mukatab then faces a choice.
If the master had other property, the tadbir would be executed from that property, and the kitabah might continue normally.
3
Locate the Two Options
The text presents two options for the mukatab: either he 'incapacitates himself' (i.e., abandons the kitabah) and becomes mudabbar, or he continues with the kitabah and pays two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the substitute (the kitabah amount).
The two-thirds figure is because the tadbir consumes one-third of the master's estate, reducing the kitabah proportionally.
4
Follow the Proof Chain regarding 'Aqr
The passage addresses a potential objection: that the 'aqr (dower for intercourse with a slave woman) is established by intercourse, not by purchase, so the master's permission to trade (for the mukatab) should not make the 'aqr owed to the master. The response uses a causal chain: kitabah necessitated purchase, purchase necessitated the falling of the hadd penalty for zina, and the falling of the hadd necessitated the 'aqr. Thus, kitabah indirectly necessitates 'aqr.
This chain distinguishes kitabah from marriage, where no such causal link exists.
5
Distinguish Kitabah from Marriage
The commentator clarifies that the causal chain does not apply to marriage because marriage does not involve purchase from the master. The 'aqr in kitabah is uniquely linked to the transfer of ownership.
This distinction is derived from al-Binaya, al-Inaya, and al-Diraya as transmitted by al-Jalabi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح تدبير مكاتبه ، وعَجْزُ نفسه وكان مُدَبَّراً ، أو مضى عليها وسعى في ثلثي قيمته ، أو ثلثي البدل إن مات سيده فقيراً فلا ينتظمه الكتابة، ولقائل أن يقول : إن العقر يثبت بالوطء لا بالشراء، والإذن بالشراء ليس إذناً بالوطء والوطء ليس من التجارة في شيء، فلا يكون ثابتاً في حق المولى. وصح تدبير مكاتبه ، وعَجْزُ نفسه وكان مُدَبَّراً ، أو مضى عليها وسعى في ثلثي قيمته ، أو ثلثي البدل إن مات سيده فقيراً : أي له الخيار : إما أن عجز نفسه وكان مدبراً، أو مضى على الكتابة. وتقرير الفرق الذي أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : والفرق أنه.... الخ أن الكتابة أوجبت الشراء، والشراء أوجب سقوط الحد، وسقوط الحد أوجب العقر، فالكتابة أوجبت العقر، ولا كذلك النكاح. كذا نقل الجلبي عن «البناية»، و«العناية»، «الدراية».
And the tadbir of his mukatab is valid, and he incapacitates himself while he was mudabbar, or he continues upon it and pays two-thirds of his value, or two-thirds of the substitute if his master dies poor, so kitabah does not encompass it. And one may say: indeed the 'aqr is established by intercourse, not by purchase, and permission for purchase is not permission for intercourse, and intercourse is not part of commerce at all, so it is not established in the right of the master. And the tadbir of his mukatab is valid, and he incapacitates himself while he was mudabbar, or he continues upon it and pays two-thirds of his value, or two-thirds of the substitute if his master dies poor: Meaning he has the choice: either he incapacitates himself and becomes mudabbar, or he continues upon kitabah. And the explanation of the difference that the commentator indicated by his saying: 'The difference is that...' etc., is that kitabah necessitated purchase, purchase necessitated the falling of the hadd penalty, falling of the hadd necessitated the 'aqr, so kitabah necessitated the 'aqr, but not so marriage. This is transmitted by al-Jalabi from al-Binaya, al-Inaya, al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah regarding the validity of tadbir on a mukatab and the options available to the mukatab when the master dies poor. The text first states that if a master makes his mukatab a mudabbar, then the mukatab has the option: either to declare himself incapacitated and become mudabbar, or to continue on the kitabah contract and pay two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the written substitute if the master dies with no other property. The commentary explains that the kitabah contract does not encompass this option; the tadbir takes effect despite the kitabah. Then a possible objection is raised: the 'aqr (dower for intercourse with a slave) is established by intercourse, not by purchase, but the master's permission to trade does not imply permission to have intercourse, so the 'aqr should not be owed to the master. The response, based on a chain of reasoning, is that the 'aqr is ultimately linked to the purchase because without purchase, intercourse would be clearly forbidden, so the 'aqr is established in the master's favor. The passage ends by clarifying the difference between kitabah and marriage regarding this causal chain.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by the master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted kitabah, an agreement to pay a specified sum for gradual emancipation.
عقر ('aqr): A dower paid to a slave woman for intercourse, analogous to mahr for a free woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He is automatically free.
D) He must choose only mudabbar.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir of a mukatab is valid, and upon the master's death with no other property, the mukatab may choose to become mudabbar or continue kitabah at two-thirds of the amount.

Validity of Kitaba for an Umm Walad and Its Consequences
Confirms validity and explains effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a kitaba contract for an umm walad is valid, and explain the legal consequences upon the master's death including the dropping of the kitaba price and the retention of earnings and children for her.

Core Idea
A kitaba for an umm walad is valid and brings immediate benefits, but upon the master's death she is freed without payment.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the validity of writing a kitaba for an umm walad. Although the umm walad is already entitled to freedom upon her master's death, the kitaba serves a practical need during his lifetime. We will explore the reasoning (istihsan) behind this permissibility and the precise consequences when the master dies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the Hanafi position is. The act is writing a kitaba for an umm walad. The ruling: it is valid (jai'iz).
The text states 'wa kitaba umm waladihi' meaning the kitaba of his umm walad is valid.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
Identify the evidence used. The proof is istihsan based on need and absence of contradiction. The umm walad needs the benefits of kitaba (immediate ownership of her hand and potential freedom upon payment) before the master's death, just like other slaves. There is no contradiction with her status because she is not yet free.
The commentary explains: 'because the kitaba is a means to obtain ownership of the hand immediately and freedom upon payment... and the need of the umm walad is like the need of others'.
3
Explain the consequences upon the master's death
When the master dies, the umm walad is freed by virtue of her status (istilad). The kitaba price is dropped because the purpose of freedom is achieved without payment. The kitaba contract becomes void to avoid futility. However, the kitaba remains effective regarding her earnings and children: they become hers and her children are freed.
The text says: 'her freedom is tied to the master's death, and the kitaba price falls... However, earnings and children are awarded to her.'
4
Note the relation to the mudabbar
The same ruling applies to a mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred). The kitaba for a mudabbar is also valid because tadbir only gives entitlement to freedom, not actual freedom, so there is no conflict.
The commentary cites Hashiyat al-Halabi: 'there is no contradiction between kitaba and tadbir because tadbir establishes only entitlement, not reality.'
5
Cite the authority
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah, affirmed by al-Hidayah and later commentaries.
The text references al-Hidayah: 'Thus in al-Hidayah.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكتابة أم ولده فعتقت بموته مجاناً ومدبره : أي صحت كتابة مدبره عتق هذا الولد وبطل عنه السعاية ؛ لأنه بمنزلة أم الولد إذ هو ولدها فيتبعها). قوله : وكتابة أمّ ولده ؛ أي وصح كتابة أم ولده ؛ لأنّ الكتابة يتوسل بها إلى ملك اليد في الحال، والحرية عند أداء البدل، وحاجة أم الولد إلى استفادة هذا المعنى قبل موت المولى، كحاجة غيرها فكان جائزاً. قوله : مجاناً ؛ أي بالاستيلاد، وتعلّق عتقها بموت السيد، وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة ؛ لأن الغرض من إيجاب البدل العتق عند الأداء، فإذا عتقت قبل الأداء لا يمكن توفير الغرض على المولى، فسقط بدل الكتابة، وبطلت الكتابة ؛ لامتناع إبقائها بلا فائدة. غير أنه تُسلّم لها الأكساب والأولاد ؛ لأنّ الكتابة انفسخت في حق البدل وبقيت في حق الأولاد والأكساب، حتى يعتق الأولاد ويخلص له الأكساب. كذا في «الهداية». قوله : صحت ... الخ ؛ لوجود المقتضى وهو الحاجة، فإنّ الثابت بالتدبير مجرَّدُ استحقاق الحرية لا حقيقتها، ولانتفاء المانع، وهو عدم المنافاة بين الكتابة والتدبير. كذا في «حاشية الجلبي»
And the kitaba of his umm walad, so she becomes free at his death gratuitously, and [the kitaba of] his mudabbar: meaning the kitaba of his mudabbar is valid. This child is freed and pursuit against him is voided; because he is like the umm walad as he is her child and follows her. His statement: 'And the kitaba of his umm walad' means the kitaba of the umm walad is valid, because the kitaba is a means to obtain ownership of the hand immediately and freedom upon payment of the price, and the need of the umm walad to obtain this meaning before the master's death is like the need of others, so it was permissible. His statement: 'gratuitously' meaning by istilad, and her freedom is tied to the master's death, and the kitaba price falls from her; because the purpose of imposing the price is freedom at the time of payment, so if she becomes free before payment, it is impossible to realize the purpose for the master, so the kitaba price falls, and the kitaba becomes void to avoid keeping it without benefit. However, earnings and children are awarded to her; because the kitaba is dissolved with respect to the price but remains with respect to children and earnings, so that the children become free and earnings become clear for her. Thus in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'it is valid' etc. due to the existence of the requisite, which is need, and because what is established by tadbir is merely the entitlement to freedom, not its reality, and due to the absence of a hindrance, which is the lack of contradiction between kitaba and tadbir. Thus in Hashiyat al-Halabi.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling confirming the validity of writing a kitaba (contract of manumission) for an umm walad (a female slave who has borne a child to her master). The text first states that if an umm walad is given a kitaba, she becomes free at her master's death without payment, and similarly the kitaba of a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred to after the master's death) is valid. The commentary explains the reason: kitaba is a means to obtain immediate ownership of the slave's hand (power over her work) and freedom upon payment. The umm walad needs this benefit before the master's death, just like other slaves, so it is permissible. When the master dies, she is freed by virtue of being umm walad, so the kitaba price is dropped because the purpose (freedom) is achieved without payment. The kitaba contract becomes void to avoid being futile. However, the kitaba remains effective with respect to her earnings and children: her children are freed and her earnings become hers. The commentary also cites al-Hidayah for this. Finally, it clarifies that kitaba for a mudabbar is valid because tadbir only gives entitlement to freedom, not actual freedom, so there is no contradiction between the two contracts.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master and is entitled to freedom upon his death.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between master and slave whereby the slave pays a sum to the master in installments in exchange for freedom.
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by the master that a slave will be free after the master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is deferred until after the master's death by a declaration of tadbir.

Key Takeaway
A kitaba for an umm walad is valid and beneficial during the master's lifetime; upon his death, she is freed without payment, but her earnings and children become hers.

Mukatab's Obligation When Master Dies Insolvent: Three Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on amount and choice for mukatab payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on the mukatab's payment upon the master's insolvent death and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
The mukatab's payment amount and choice depend on divisibility of emancipation and allocation of the kitabah debt.

When a master dies insolvent and his only asset is a mukatab slave, the mukatab must continue paying towards freedom. But how much? The Hanafi school has three distinct views on both the amount and whether the mukatab has a choice. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, grounding the dispute in principles of emancipation divisibility and debt allocation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and disputed issues
The master dies insolvent, leaving only the mukatab as asset. The mukatab is both a slave (partially freed by tadbir) and a debtor (kitabah). The dispute covers two issues: the amount to pay and whether the mukatab has a choice between two options.
Remember: tadbir frees one-third of the slave from the master's estate.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa: the mukatab may choose between paying two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah. Reasoning: emancipation is divisible, so two-thirds remain slave; two payments are due (immediate by tadbir, deferred by kitabah), hence a choice.
Divisibility (tajazzu') is key: the slave is partially freed, partially slave.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf: the mukatab pays the lesser of two-thirds value or full kitabah, no choice. Reasoning: the entire slave is freed by tadbir (since the master has no other assets), so only one payment is due. The mukatab naturally chooses the lesser, giving no meaningful choice.
Whole emancipation collapses the choice; one obligation remains.
4
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and reasoning
Muhammad: the mukatab pays the lesser of two-thirds value or two-thirds kitabah, no choice. Reasoning: the kitabah is for the whole slave, but tadbir frees one-third, so one-third of the debt falls. Thus only two-thirds of the debt remains, and since the slave is wholly free, no choice exists.
The debt is reduced proportionally to the freed portion.
5
Compare the practical outcomes (thamarah al-khilaf)
The differences are real. Example: value = 1200, kitabah = 1000. Abu Hanifa: choose between 800 (2/3 of value) or 1000. Abu Yusuf: pay 800 (lesser). Muhammad: pay the lesser of 800 (2/3 value) or 667 (2/3 kitabah) = 667. The amount and choice vary.
Each view is defensible within the madhhab; the passage does not declare a mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب تصرفاته وعجزه وأحكامه
ويسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو كلِّ البدل في موتِ سيده معسراً
. [1]
(ويسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو كلِّ البدل في موتِ سيده معسراً)، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وعند أبي يوسف الله يسعى في الأقلّ منهما، وعند محمد له يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة أو ثلثي البدل ، أما الخيار وعدمه ففرعُ التَّجزؤ وعدمه كما مر.
وأما المقدار فمحمد الله يقول : البدلُ لما كان مقابلاً بالكل فبالموت يسلّمُ له ثلث البدل، ومن المحال أن يجب البدلُ في مقابلة الثلث وهما يقولان : البدلُ وقع في مقابلة الثلثين، لأنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أنَّ الإنسانَ لا يلتزم المالَ في مقابلة ما يستحق حريته. ١ ] قوله : ويسعى في ثلثي قيمته...الخ ؛ أي إن مات المولى ولا مال له غيرها، فهي بالخيار بين أن تسعى في ثلثي قيمتها أو جميع مال الكتابة، وإنما قيد بقوله : معسراً ؛ أي لا مال له غيرها ؛ لأنه لو كان له مال غيرها وهي تخرج من ثلث المال عتقت بالتدبير وسقطت عنها المكاتبة ؛ لوقوع الاستغناء بها عن أداء المال، فكان هذا بمنزلة ما لو عتق المولى مكاتبه. كذا في «الكفاية»).
[٢]قوله : يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة أو ثلثي البدل، فالخلاف في الخيار والمقدار، فأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة الله في المقدار، ومع محمد له في نفي الخيار، أما الخيار ففرع تجزؤ الإعتاق، والإعتاق عنده لما تجزأ بقي الثلثان رقيقاً، وقد تلقتها جهتا حرية ببدلين : معجّلة بالتدبير ومؤجّلة بالكتابة فتخير، وعندهما لما عتق كلها . بعضها فهي حرّة، ووجب عليها أحد المالين، فتختار الأقل لا محالة، فلا معنى للتخيير. وأما المقدار ؛ فلمحمد الله أنه قابل البدل بالكل، قد سلم لها الثلث بالتدبير، فمن المحال أن يجب البدل بمقابلته ، ألا ترى أنه لو سلّم لها الكل بأن خرجت من الثلث بعتق يسقط كل البدل ، فهاهنا يسقط الثلث، فصار كما إذا تأخر التدبير عن الكتابة. ولهما : أن جميع البدل مقابل بثلثي رقبتها ، فلا يسقط منه شيء ؛ وهذا لأنّ البدل وإن قوبل بالكلّ صورة وصيغة ، لكنّه مقيّد لما ذكرنا معنى وإرادة ؛ لأنها استحقت حرية الثلث ظاهراً، والظاهر أنّ الإنسان لا يلتزم المال بمقابلة ما يستحق حرية. هكذا في «الهداية»(1).
Book of the Mukatab: His transactions, incapacity, and rulings. And he (the mukatab) must work for two-thirds of his value or the entire deferred payment upon the death of his master who is insolvent. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, he works for the lesser of the two. According to Muhammad, he works for the lesser of two-thirds of the value or two-thirds of the deferred payment. As for the choice and its absence, it is a branch of divisibility and its absence as mentioned. As for the amount, Muhammad says: Since the payment is in exchange for the whole, by death one-third of the payment is waived for him, and it is impossible for the payment to be required in exchange for one-third. They (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say: The payment is in exchange for two-thirds, because it is apparent that a person does not commit money in exchange for what he is entitled to by freedom. [1] His statement: 'and he works for two-thirds of his value...' means if the master dies and he has no other property, she (the female mukatab) has the choice between working for two-thirds of her value or the entire kitabah. He restricted it by 'insolvent' meaning he has no property other than her; because if he had other property and she comes from one-third of the estate, she would be freed by tadbir and the kitabah would fall from her due to being independent of paying the money. This is like if the master freed his mukatab. So it is in al-Kifayah. [2] His statement: 'he works for the lesser of two-thirds of the value or two-thirds of the deferred payment.' The dispute is in the choice and the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa in the amount and with Muhammad in negating choice. As for choice, it is a branch of divisibility of emancipation. According to him (Abu Hanifa), since emancipation is divisible, the two-thirds remain as slaves, and they have received two directions of freedom with two payments: immediate by tadbir and deferred by kitabah, so she has a choice. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since all of her is emancipated, she is free and one of the two payments is obligatory, so she inevitably chooses the lesser, thus no meaning for choice. As for the amount: according to Muhammad, he made the payment in exchange for the whole; one-third is already given to her by tadbir, so it is impossible for the payment to be in exchange for it. Do you not see that if the whole is given to her by being from one-third, the entire payment falls? So here one-third falls, making it as if tadbir occurred after kitabah. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): The entire payment is in exchange for two-thirds of her slave-ness, so nothing falls from it. This is because the payment, though in form and wording it is in exchange for the whole, it is restricted in meaning and intent as mentioned, because she apparently becomes entitled to freedom of one-third, and it is apparent that a person does not commit money in exchange for what is entitled to freedom. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mukatab's obligation when the master dies insolvent. The base ruling states that the mukatab must work for two-thirds of his value or the entire deferred payment (kitabah). The commentator expands by detailing three positions: Abu Hanifa gives the mukatab a choice between paying two-thirds of his value or the full kitabah. Abu Yusuf requires paying the lesser of the two options, removing the choice. Muhammad requires paying the lesser of two-thirds of the value or two-thirds of the kitabah. The dispute centers on two issues: (1) whether the mukatab has a choice (khiyar) and (2) the amount to be paid. Abu Hanifa says the mukatab has a choice because emancipation is divisible—two-thirds of the slave remains in slavery, so two payments are due (one immediate by tadbir, one deferred by kitabah), hence a choice. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad deny choice because the entire slave is emancipated (the tadbir applies to all of her), so only one payment is due, and the mukatab naturally chooses the lesser. On amount, Muhammad argues the payment is for the whole slave, so tadbir already frees one-third, thus one-third of the debt falls. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue the payment is for two-thirds of the slave (the part not freed by tadbir), so no reduction occurs. The relied-upon position is not explicitly given in this passage, but the Hidayah summary suggests the mukatab's apparent entitlement to one-third freedom leads to the conclusion that the payment is in exchange for the remaining two-thirds.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of kitabah with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بدل (badal): The deferred payment (kitabah) agreed upon in the contract of kitabah.
تدبير (tadbir): A master's declaration that his slave will be free upon the master's death; it is a type of contingent emancipation.
تجزؤ (tajazzu'): Divisibility; here, whether emancipation can be partial or only complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, what is the mukatab's obligation when his master dies insolvent?
A) Pay two-thirds of his value only
B) Pay the entire kitabah only
C) Pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah
D) Pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers three views on the mukatab's post-master-death payment, rooted in principles of divisibility of emancipation and allocation of the kitabah debt.

Settlement with Mukatab: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on validity of sulh with mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a settlement where a mukatab pays half immediately for a deferred debt, applying istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
The term (ajal) has quasi-monetary value for a mukatab, balancing the exchange and preventing riba.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi instance where juristic preference (istihsan) overrides strict analogy (qiyas). The issue is whether a master can settle with his mukatab for immediate payment of half the deferred kitabah. While qiyas suggests it is invalid due to apparent riba, the Hanafi school upholds it based on the unique nature of the mukatab's debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific contract? (sulh between master and mukatab for immediate half payment of deferred debt). The ruling: it is sahih (valid) according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is stated explicitly at the start.
2
Understand the objection (qiyas)
Why would qiyas consider it invalid? Because it appears to be an exchange of money for time (ajal), which is not property, leading to riba.
Qiyas draws analogy with a free person's debt settlement, which is prohibited.
3
Examine the istihsan reasoning
The Hanafi school invokes istihsan: for the mukatab, the deferred term has monetary value in one respect (mal min wajh), since he cannot pay without it. The kitabah payment itself is not full property (not property in all respects), as shown by the fact that kafala (guarantee) is not valid for it. Thus, the exchange is between two property-like entities, and since the types differ, no riba occurs.
The balance (i'tidal) between the two sides removes the prohibition.
4
Identify the scope of the ruling
This ruling is specific to the mukatab. It does not apply to a free person (hurr) or to a mukatab of another (mukatab al-ghayr).
The limitation is explicitly mentioned in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلحه مع مكاتبه على نصف حال من بدل مؤجل
[1]
(وصلحه مع مكاتبه على نصف حال من بدل مؤجل) : أي صح صلحه ، والقياس أن لا يصح ، لأَنَّهُ اعتياض عن الأجل بالمال، ووجه الاستحسان : أن الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه لا يقدر على الأداء إلا به، وبدل الكتابة ليس بمال من وجه حتى لا تصح الكفالة به فاعتدلا .
[0]
[١]قوله : أن لا يصح؛ لأنّه اعتياض عن الأجل، وهو ليس بمال، والدين مال فكان ربا؛ ولهذا لا يجوز مثله في الحرّ، بأن كان على الحرّ ألف مؤجّل فصالحه على خمس مئة حالة، وفي مكاتب الغير بأن كان على مكاتب الغير ألف إلى سنة فصالحه على خمسمئة. كذا في بعض حواشي «الهداية».
[٢] قوله : ليس بمال من وجه ؛ لاحتمال التعجيز.
[٣]قوله : حتى لا تصح الكفالة به؛ أي ببدل الكتابة، فلو كان مالاً من كل وجه لصحت الكفالة به. كذا في شرح العيني).
[٤] قوله : فاعتدلا ؛ فكان اعتياضاً عما هو مال من وجه بما هو مال من وجه، واختلف الجنس، فلم يكن ثمة ربا. كذا في «العناية».
And his settlement with his mukatab for half immediate from a deferred payment. [1] (And his settlement with his mukatab for half immediate from a deferred payment) meaning: his settlement is valid, and the qiyas is that it should not be valid, because it is an exchange of money for the term. The istihsan is: because the term is in the right of the mukatab property in one respect, as he cannot pay except with it, and the kitabah payment is not property in one respect such that kafala with it is not valid, so they balanced each other. [0] [1] His statement: 'it should not be valid' because it is an exchange for the term, which is not property, and the debt is property, so it would be riba. Therefore a similar thing is not permitted for a free person, e.g., if a free person had a deferred thousand and he settled for immediate five hundred, nor for a mukatab of another. [2] His statement: 'not property in one respect' due to possibility of incapacitation. [3] His statement: 'such that kafala with it is not valid' meaning with the kitabah payment; if it were property in all respects, kafala with it would be valid. [4] His statement: 'balanced each other' so it was an exchange of what is property in one respect for what is property in one respect, and the types differed, so there was no riba.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a sulh (settlement) between a master and his mukatab, where the mukatab pays half of the deferred kitabah immediately. The qiyas (analogical reasoning) would deem this invalid because it appears to be an exchange of money for the time period (ajal), which is not a real property, thus resembling riba. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to uphold its validity. The reasoning is that for the mukatab, the deferred term has a monetary value in one respect, as he cannot pay without it being deferred. On the other hand, the kitabah payment itself is not considered full property (mal) in every respect, as it is contingent on the mukatab's ability to work. For example, kafala (guarantee) is not valid for the kitabah debt. Thus, the exchange is one of a property-like thing (the immediate payment) for another property-like thing (the term), and since they differ in type, there is no riba. The commentary also notes that if this settlement were attempted with a free person, it would be invalid due to clear riba. The difference lies in the unique nature of the mukatab's contract, where time has a quasi-monetary value.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise where one party pays something to discharge a debt or obligation.
أجل (ajal): Deferred time period; in kitabah, the time allowed for payment.
مال من وجه (mal min wajh): Property in one respect; something that has some monetary characteristics but not fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the master and mukatab consented freely
B) Because the deferred term has monetary value for the mukatab and the kitabah debt is not full property
C) Because the settlement is a form of charity
D) Because the qiyas is weak

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates sulh with a mukatab for early payment of a reduced amount because the term has quasi-monetary value for the mukatab and the kitabah debt is not full property, preventing riba.

Kitabah by a Sick Master: Heirs' Right to Reject Deferred Payment
Ruling on sick master's kitabah at double value upon death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick master's kitabah at inflated price and explain the heirs' right to reject the deferred term based on the one-third limit.

Core Idea
A sick master's kitabah at double value is valid, but heirs can reject the deferred term because the deferment is a gift exceeding one-third.

When a terminally ill master writes a kitabah for his slave at double the market value with deferred payment, the contract is valid. However, because the master's disposals are limited to one-third of his estate, the heirs have the right to reject the deferred term. The mukatab then faces a choice: pay the full inflated price immediately or pay only the slave's current value. This lesson explores the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the kitabah contract made by a terminally ill master. The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih) but subject to the heirs' approval of the deferred term.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle that a sick person's transactions are limited to one-third of the estate, based on the hadith: 'Allah has granted you one-third of your wealth in charity.'
This principle applies to gifts and bequests, including gratuitous deferments.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The deferment of payment is a gift of time with monetary value. Since the master has no other property, the gift of deferment exceeds the one-third limit, giving heirs the right to reject it.
The slave's value is 1000, kitabah is 2000; the deferment's value is the opportunity cost, effectively 1000 – the excess over value.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the deferred term as a binding contract term, not a gift, and thus not subject to the one-third limitation.
The conflict hinges on whether the deferment is viewed as a gratuitous concession or an integral part of the sale.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because the deferment clearly has value and the sick person's gratuitous acts are restricted. The mukatab is given an option to pay the slave's value to avoid hardship.
This ruling is established in Zahir al-Riwayah and confirmed in later texts.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a terminally ill master who writes a kitabah contract for his slave at double the slave's market value, with deferred payment. The master then dies, leaving no other property. The heirs have the right to reject the deferred term because the sick person's actions in the illness of death are considered limited to one-third of the estate. The commentary from Hashiyat al-Jalabi explains the scenario: the slave is worth 1000, but the kitabah is for 2000 payable in one year. Upon the master's death, the heirs can demand immediate payment or cancel the deferment because the master's gift of the deferment is a disposal that exceeds his one-third limit. The mukatab then may have a choice: pay the full 2000 immediately or the slave's value (1000) effectively becoming free. The exact ruling is not fully detailed in the OCR, but the key point is that the sick person's disposal in the kitabah is subject to the heirs' approval. The footnotes refer to standard Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
مريض (marid): A person in his terminal illness (marad al-mawt).
ضعف القيمة (di'f al-qimah): Double the slave's market value; indicates the inflated price in the kitabah.

Key Takeaway
A sick master's kitabah at inflated price is valid, but heirs can reject the deferred term because the deferment is a gift subject to the one-third limit.

The Mukatab of a Terminally Ill Master: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Expansion on the kitaba ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the mukatab's obligation when the master dies terminally ill, and apply the mufta bihi position to compute the immediate payment.

Core Idea
The entire deferred sum is the substitute for the slave's person, so deferment beyond one-third is void.

When a terminally ill master writes a kitaba and dies, the deceased's estate is limited to one-third for such transactions. The slave's deferred payment is treated as a substitute for his person. The Hanafi masters differ on what portion the slave must pay immediately: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say two-thirds of the deferred sum; Muhammad says two-thirds of the slave's value. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
A terminally ill master dies after writing a mukataba for a deferred sum. The slave had been promised freedom upon full payment. The heirs now have a claim. The core question is: what must the slave pay immediately to keep the contract alive?
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf vs. Imam Muhammad).
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The slave must pay two-thirds of the full deferred sum immediately, and the remaining one-third remains deferred. If he refuses, he is enslaved.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
The slave must pay two-thirds of the slave's value immediately, and the remainder up to the full deferred sum is deferred. If he refuses, he is enslaved.
Muhammad's reasoning: the sick person cannot defer more than one-third of the value, but can abandon the excess.
4
Analyze the evidence behind each position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that the entire deferred sum is the substitute (badal) for the slave's person (mubdal). The heirs' right attaches to the substitute, so deferment is a waiver of their right, effective only from one-third. Muhammad argues that the sick person can abandon the excess amount (i.e., the difference between the deferred sum and the value), so he can also defer it.
The commentary also distinguishes from khul' (divorce for compensation) where the compensation is not a substitute for property.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the amount immediately due. Per the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the immediate payment is two-thirds of the full deferred sum; per Muhammad, it is two-thirds of the slave's value. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This also applies when the deferred sum is exactly half the value (the second scenario in the text).

Source Text

[1]
.
ورد ورثته أدى ثلثي البدل حالاً ، وباقيه مؤجلاً ، أو استرق) : أي خير العبد بين أن يؤدي ثلثي البدل حالاً والباقي" مؤجلاً، وبين أن يمتنع فيسترق ، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وعند محمد الله خير العبدُ بين أن يؤدِّي ثلثي القيمة حالاً ، والباقي إلى تمام البدل مؤجّلاً، وبين أن يمتنع فيسترق ؛ لأنَّ المريض ليس له التأجيلُ في ثلثي القيمة ، أما فيما وراءه " يصح له الترك فيصح له التأخير، لهما : أن جميع المسمّى بدلُ الرَّقبة وحق الورثة متعلّق بالمبدل، فكذا بالبدل ، فلا يصح له التَّأخير إلا في ثلثه.
دفعاً لضرر تأخير حقهم إلى مضي الأجل عن أنفسهم. [1] قوله : ثلثي البدل ؛ وهو ألف وثلاثمئة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهماً وثلث درهم في الصورة المذكورة ). (۲) قوله : والباقي ؛ هو ست مئة وستة وستون درهماً ، وثلثا درهم" [٣) قوله : فيما وراءه ؛ أي الزائد على ثلثي القيمة (۳).
(۲)
[٤]قوله : يصح له الترك ؛ بأن يترك الزيادة ويكاتبه على قيمته ؛ لأنه لم يتعلق بها حق الورثة، فيصح له التأخير؛ لأنه لما جاز له ترك أصله جاز له تركُ وصفه وهو التعجيل بالطريق الأولى، فصار كما إذا خالع المريض امرأته على ألف إلى سنة جاز ؛ لأنَّ له أن يطلقها بغير بدل. [0]قوله : بدل الرقبة ؛ من حيث أنّه لا يعتقُ إلا بأداء الكل، حتى أجرى عليها أحكام الإبدال، وحق الورثة متعلّق بالمبدل، فكذا بالبدل، والتأجيل إسقاط معنى، فيعتبر من ثلث الجميع، بخلاف الخلع ؛ لأنَّ البدل فيه لا يقابل المال، فلم يتعلّق حق الورثة بالمبدل، فلا يتعلّق بالبدل. كذا في «الهداية»(4).

Book of the Mukatab: His transactions, incapacity, and rulings. [29] If his heirs come, he pays two-thirds of the deferred payment immediately, and the remainder deferred, or he is enslaved. And in the case where the payment is half the value, he pays two-thirds of it immediately or is enslaved. [Commentary: He is given the choice to pay two-thirds of the deferred immediately and the remainder deferred, or refuse and be enslaved. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he is given the choice between paying two-thirds of the value immediately and the remainder up to the full deferred amount deferred, or refuse and be enslaved, because the sick person does not have the right to defer two-thirds of the value, but beyond that he may abandon (the excess) so he may defer. Their argument: the entire specified sum is the substitute for the slave's person, and the heirs' right pertains to the substituted thing, thus also to the substitute, so he cannot defer except for one-third. To prevent the harm of delaying their right until the term expires. [Marginal notes] ... [30] In the case where the payment is half the value here, he pays two-thirds of it immediately or is enslaved. Because the favor (muhabah) pertains to the amount and to the deferment, so it is executed from one-third, not two-thirds, by agreement. If a free man says to the master of a slave: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for such-and-such, and stipulate that he is freed upon paying it first,' and he does so, and the free man pays, the slave is freed, and he does not have recourse. (Commentary: He does not have recourse against the slave because he is a volunteer in payment. The slave is freed only by the free man's payment. If he stipulated freedom upon his payment, it is obvious; if he did not stipulate, analogy would say the slave is not freed unless he consented, but by istihsan he is freed because the contract is suspended on his acceptance...)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of the mukatab (a slave who has contracted manumission for a deferred payment) when his master dies while terminally ill. It also discusses the case where a free unrelated person pays the kitaba on behalf of the slave. The commentary is from Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. 

The first ruling: If a terminally ill master dies after writing a mukataba for a deferred payment, and the payment exceeds one-third of his estate (the maximum bequest allowed to a non-heir), then the heirs have a claim. The slave is given a choice: either pay two-thirds of the deferred amount immediately and the rest remain deferred, or refuse and be enslaved. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs: he says the slave pays two-thirds of the slave's value (not the full deferred sum) immediately, and the remainder up to the full deferred sum is deferred, or else the slave is enslaved. The reason: a terminally ill person cannot defer a payment that exceeds one-third of his estate, but he can abandon the excess altogether; since he can abandon, he can also defer by priority. The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the entire specified deferred sum is a substitute for the slave's person (badal al-raqaba). The heirs' right is attached to the person (mubdal), so it attaches to the substitute as well. Deferring the payment is akin to waiving a right, which is only effective from one-third of the entire property. They differentiate from the case of khul' (divorce for compensation) because there the compensation is not against a property right. 

The second scenario: when the deferred payment is exactly half the slave's value, and the master dies. Here, the favor (muhabah) is in both the amount (discount) and the deferment, so it is effective only from one-third, not two-thirds, by agreement. The slave must pay two-thirds of the value immediately or be enslaved. 

Then the text introduces a separate rule: If a free person (ajnabi, outsider) tells a master to write a kitaba for his slave for a specified amount, and stipulates that the slave will be freed upon that person's payment, and the master does so and the free person pays, then the slave is freed, and the payer cannot reclaim the amount from the slave because he is a volunteer (mutabarri'). If the free person did not stipulate freedom upon his payment, then by qiyas the slave would not be freed without his own agreement; but by istihsan, the slave is freed because the contract is suspended and becomes effective upon payment, as explained further in other texts.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitaba with his master to earn and pay a specified sum in installments for his freedom.
البدل (al-badal): The deferred payment amount specified in the kitaba contract, which serves as the substitute (badal) for the slave's person.
المحاباة (al-muhabah): The favor or discount given by the master in the kitaba, whether by reducing the amount or by granting deferment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a terminally ill master dies after writing a kitaba for 3000 dirhams, what is the immediate payment required from the slave?
A) 2000 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) 3000 dirhams
D) Two-thirds of the slave's value

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the mukatab must pay two-thirds of the full deferred sum immediately, based on the principle that the deferred sum is the substitute for the slave's person and deferment beyond one-third is void.

beginner

Free Person Paying the Kitaba: Volunteering and Its Consequences
Ruling on a third party paying the kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a free person pays the kitaba on behalf of a slave, and explain why the payer has no recourse.

Core Idea
A volunteer payer cannot reclaim from the slave because his payment is a donation.

If a free, unrelated person (ajnabi) requests a master to write a kitaba for his slave and then pays the sum, the slave is freed, but the payer cannot reclaim the amount from the slave. This ruling is based on the principle that the payer is a volunteer (mutabarri'). This lesson also covers the distinction between stipulating freedom upon payment and not, where istihsan overrides qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
A free person (ajnabi) tells a master: 'Write a kitaba for your slave for such-and-such amount, and stipulate that he is freed upon my payment.' The master does so, and the free person pays. The slave is freed.
Alternatively, he may not stipulate freedom upon his payment, but the ruling is similar.
2
State the ruling on the payer's right to reclaim
The payer has no recourse (does not reclaim) against the slave because he is a volunteer (mutabarri'). His payment is a donation on his part, not a loan.
This is regardless of whether the kitaba contract was conditional on his payment or not.
3
Analyze the scenario without stipulation
If the free person did not stipulate that the slave is freed upon his payment, analogy (qiyas) would say the slave is not freed because the contract was not conditional on his payment; the slave's consent is required. However, istihsan prevails: the slave is freed because the contract is considered suspended on the slave's acceptance, and the payment perfects it.
This is an example of istihsan overriding qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Identify the legal principle
The core principle is that a volunteer's payment does not create a right of reimbursement against the beneficiary unless it was a loan or with his request. Here, the payer acted voluntarily, so he cannot reclaim.
This aligns with the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions).
5
Contrast with similar cases
If the slave himself had requested the free person to pay on his behalf, then the payer could reclaim. But in the scenario, the free person initiated the request to the master, not the slave.
This nuance is not in the text but is a natural extension.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of the mukatab (a slave who has contracted manumission for a deferred payment) when his master dies while terminally ill. It also discusses the case where a free unrelated person pays the kitaba on behalf of the slave. The commentary is from Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. 

The first ruling: If a terminally ill master dies after writing a mukataba for a deferred payment, and the payment exceeds one-third of his estate (the maximum bequest allowed to a non-heir), then the heirs have a claim. The slave is given a choice: either pay two-thirds of the deferred amount immediately and the rest remain deferred, or refuse and be enslaved. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs: he says the slave pays two-thirds of the slave's value (not the full deferred sum) immediately, and the remainder up to the full deferred sum is deferred, or else the slave is enslaved. The reason: a terminally ill person cannot defer a payment that exceeds one-third of his estate, but he can abandon the excess altogether; since he can abandon, he can also defer by priority. The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the entire specified deferred sum is a substitute for the slave's person (badal al-raqaba). The heirs' right is attached to the person (mubdal), so it attaches to the substitute as well. Deferring the payment is akin to waiving a right, which is only effective from one-third of the entire property. They differentiate from the case of khul' (divorce for compensation) because there the compensation is not against a property right. 

The second scenario: when the deferred payment is exactly half the slave's value, and the master dies. Here, the favor (muhabah) is in both the amount (discount) and the deferment, so it is effective only from one-third, not two-thirds, by agreement. The slave must pay two-thirds of the value immediately or be enslaved. 

Then the text introduces a separate rule: If a free person (ajnabi, outsider) tells a master to write a kitaba for his slave for a specified amount, and stipulates that the slave will be freed upon that person's payment, and the master does so and the free person pays, then the slave is freed, and the payer cannot reclaim the amount from the slave because he is a volunteer (mutabarri'). If the free person did not stipulate freedom upon his payment, then by qiyas the slave would not be freed without his own agreement; but by istihsan, the slave is freed because the contract is suspended and becomes effective upon payment, as explained further in other texts.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitaba with his master to earn and pay a specified sum in installments for his freedom.
المتبرع (al-mutabarri'): A person who voluntarily gives something without expecting compensation.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of legal reasoning that prefers a ruling that is more accommodating or just over a strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free person pays the kitaba of a slave without being asked by the slave, and without stipulating freedom upon his payment, what is the ruling?
A) The slave is not freed because there was no stipulation.
B) The slave is freed by istihsan, and the payer cannot reclaim.
C) The slave is freed only if the master agrees to the payment.
D) The slave is freed, and the payer can reclaim from the master.

Key Takeaway
A volunteer who pays the kitaba frees the slave but has no right to reimbursement, because his intention was donation.

Kitaba of a Female Slave with Her Young Children: Acceptance of Absent Child is Void
Ruling on acceptance of kitaba by a female slave for herself and her young children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the acceptance of an absent minor in a kitaba contract is void (laghw) and explain that the contract binds only the present slave, not the absent children.

Core Idea
A kitaba contract only binds those present and legally competent; the acceptance of an absent minor is void.

In a kitaba contract, the master offers manumission in exchange for payment. When a female slave is given kitaba together with her young children, only she is present and competent to accept. The acceptance of her absent children—or acceptance on their behalf—has no legal effect. This lesson examines the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states: 'The acceptance of the absent one is void.' Note that this is a general principle: acceptance from someone not present at the contract is ineffective.
2
Understand the scenario
The scenario: a female slave and her two young children are given kitaba. She accepts for herself and on their behalf. The ruling distinguishes between her acceptance (valid for her) and the children's acceptance (void).
3
Analyze the reasoning
The children are 'absent' because they lack legal capacity due to minority. Their acceptance or rejection has no effect. The contract only binds the present slave (mother). The mother's acceptance does not obligate the children.
4
Connect to analogous cases
The commentator compares this to a guarantee (kafala) where someone guarantees for another without his order; the guarantor is not bound. The acceptance of the absent does not change the ruling.
5
Derive the practical consequence
If the mother pays the kitaba, it discharges her debt. If a child pays, he is a volunteer and cannot recover from the mother or sibling. The master must accept payment from any of them.
